  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f64d8002-5ae5-4f72-8e5c-83ecd3bee385'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2096443435?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=popular">popular</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=decent-enough">decent-enough</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=pretty-good">pretty-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=unfunny">unfunny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096443435" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15083914323899071754">I gave the book 3.5 score but rounded it to 3 stars. I love giving 3 stars to books that I think deserve so, yet I feel that I'm underestimating them. 3 star books are mercurial in their very being. I happen to think that the author is her own worst enemy.<br/><br/>Whenever a clash is about to occur, or when there's tension and drama and pathos in the present reading of a particular chapter, The author changes the scene and I am left with the feeling that nothing is resolved. <br/><br/>There is a large cast of char</span>
  <span id="freeText15083914323899071754" style="display:none">I gave the book 3.5 score but rounded it to 3 stars. I love giving 3 stars to books that I think deserve so, yet I feel that I'm underestimating them. 3 star books are mercurial in their very being. I happen to think that the author is her own worst enemy.<br /><br />Whenever a clash is about to occur, or when there's tension and drama and pathos in the present reading of a particular chapter, The author changes the scene and I am left with the feeling that nothing is resolved. <br /><br />There is a large cast of characters in the book. Some of them are drawn with hasty, economic lines, and I thought it was a shame that the author cannot do justice to all. Finally I thought that the climax was fascinating, but not epic. There is a power struggle going on in the book, and it will temporarily resolve itself after each book. Then it's back to square one. I have a lot to say about this book, but I must conclude that the flaws cannot be ignored.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15083914323899071754" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_134795994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134795994" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134795994?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134795994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3143743983586162934">Sometimes, though you know it to be true, nature will remind you of what a bitch it is.<br/><br/>Like, for example, if you come to Australia and manage to avoid the myriad of poisonous spiders, snakes, scorpions, jelly fish, stone fish and some frogs. <br/><br/>Then you manage to not get killed or viciously maimed by the crocodiles, koalas, cassowary, dingos, sharks, sting-rays and locals (do you have any idea of how many tourists go missing and get murdered in Australia?)<br/><br/>Then you survive the outback with its inten</span>
  <span id="freeText3143743983586162934" style="display:none">Sometimes, though you know it to be true, nature will remind you of what a bitch it is.<br><br>Like, for example, if you come to Australia and manage to avoid the myriad of poisonous spiders, snakes, scorpions, jelly fish, stone fish and some frogs. <br><br>Then you manage to not get killed or viciously maimed by the crocodiles, koalas, cassowary, dingos, sharks, sting-rays and locals (do you have any idea of how many tourists go missing and get murdered in Australia?)<br><br>Then you survive the outback with its intense heat, freezing nights, lack of water, flash floods, raging forest fires and travelling transvestites on a mystical journey of self-discovery. Or you make it to the ocean where you narrowly avoid our rips and hurricanes and over-zealous children...<br><br>Only to find yourself brushing up against the Gympie-Gympie tree or its five closely related cousins and finding yourself in such intense pain that you understand why horses and dogs and men have been known to throw themselves off cliff edges to make it stop. Then of course, you survive that but find the tiny, almost invisible barbs that pierced your skin weren’t properly removed and for pretty much the rest of your life, you’re likely to be in pain any time that skin comes in contact with water.<br><br>Fuck you nature!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br><i>Yeah, yeah, yeah! Damn it nature always has to have the last word!</i><br><br>So, nature doesn’t just hate you. It hates Rachel Morgan too. You see, it has allowed her to be born with absolutely no ability to think five minutes ahead to save her freakin’ life. In fact, if the universe didn’t conspire AGAINST nature in order to surround her with a group of people able to adequately formulate, prepare and execute a plan, then she would have died coming out of the woman by trying to shove herself down the doctor’s throat because it seemed like a good idea at the time.<br><br>So intriguing and wonderful is her support group, that they manage to carry this entire series and save Rachel so many times that I can only assume they’re actually robots operated by awesomified My Little Pony dolls.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342474i/698193.jpg" alt="MLP" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Probably the Master Chief My Little Pony operates Jenks.</i><br><br>I had to stop this book when I reached the part in which Rachel is, yet again, about to go into an extremely dangerous situation, with no back up, and the most half-assed plan ever conceived on the face of this earth.<br><br>I enjoy these books but if I keep reading, I’ll probably give myself severe blood-pressure problems. When I’m not pregnant and wound up tighter than a honey badger on LSD, then I’ll pick this book up and finish it. Until, then, I’ll just have to say that this series is pretty good. Not fantabulous, but pretty good.<br><br>Then again, it's probably the honey and nectar speaking. Never sugar drink and fly, kids!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380342474i/698194.jpg" alt="jenks" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3143743983586162934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351709093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4620998947163759084"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/07/mini-reviews-for-a-few-demons-more-the-outlaw-demon-wails-by-kim-harrison.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><p>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404904728i/10295018.png' alt='@!-#' width='100' height='115' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404904728i/10295019.png' alt='Vampires' width='100' height='115' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404904728i/10295020.png' alt='Epic' width='100' height='115' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404904728i/10295022.png' alt='tear' width='100' height='115' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</p><br/>So I don't know if I'm using the "@!?#" button correctly, but in my head it's the "WTF?! Elephant." Has been since I first laid eyes on it. So if that's not what it's supposed to mean, now you know what it means to me:<br/><br/>Elephant as illustration for WTF?! + @!?# (WTF?!) = WTF?! squared.<br/><br/>And that is what is going on here. And it is fan-friggin'-tastic.<br/><br/>Right. So Trent's getting married to Ellasbeth, and he wants Rachel to work security for the wedding.<br/><br/>*blinks*<br/><br/>I kno</span>
  <span id="freeText4620998947163759084" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/07/mini-reviews-for-a-few-demons-more-the-outlaw-demon-wails-by-kim-harrison.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404904728i/10295018.png" alt="@!-#" width="100" height="115" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404904728i/10295019.png" alt="Vampires" width="100" height="115" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404904728i/10295020.png" alt="Epic" width="100" height="115" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404904728i/10295022.png" alt="tear" width="100" height="115" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br>So I don't know if I'm using the "@!?#" button correctly, but in my head it's the "WTF?! Elephant." Has been since I first laid eyes on it. So if that's not what it's supposed to mean, now you know what it means to me:<br><br>Elephant as illustration for WTF?! + @!?# (WTF?!) = WTF?! squared.<br><br>And that is what is going on here. And it is fan-friggin'-tastic.<br><br>Right. So Trent's getting married to Ellasbeth, and he wants Rachel to work security for the wedding.<br><br>*blinks*<br><br>I know what you're thinking. You're thinking, "Why on earth would Trent want Rachel at his wedding?"<br><br>Well, b/c Lee RVSP-ed as his best man, and that's a problem, b/c Lee is Al's new familiar in the Ever After . . . so how's he going to pull off being the best man in Trent's wedding?<br><br>That is an excellent question.<br><br>It's also a question that has Trent understandably nervous, and as Rachel is the only person to ever hold her own against Al, Trent wants her in place to handle whatever unknown, yet inevitable, shenanigans Al is planning.<br><br>Rachel says, "Hell NO. It's my birthday."<br><br>Trent says, "40k."<br><br>Rachel says, "Well, maybe . . . but I better not have to wear an ugly dress."<br><br>B/c Rachel isn't just going to be working security from the sidelines in a Quen-like capacity, oh no, she's doing it as one of Ellasbeth's BRIDESMAIDS.<br><br>*giggle snorts*<br><br>I hadn't really thought about it before, but a fellow fan of <em>The Hollows</em> commented on one of my status updates on Goodreads that this book is a real turning point for the series. On the one hand, yeah, <em>obviously</em> (b/c the Bad Thing happens in this book).<br><br>But there is a LOT more going on than that. Al is in trouble with the demons, and he wants Rachel's help getting out of it. Ceri and Trent finally meet. Rachel upsets the balance of power between the heavy hitting Supes. Skimmer does that other Big Thing . . .<br><br>And don't let ALL THE THINGS scare you, b/c unlike <em>True Blood</em>, Season 4's hodgepodge of overwhelming randomness, <em>For a Few Demons More</em> is wonderfully coherent, and by far the best book in the series up to that point. YEP. This is where it starts getting REALLY good.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351599255" rel="nofollow noopener">Dead Witch Walking (The Hollows #1)</a>
</b><br><b>

<span id="freeTextContainer9634582825010680759">Just too much Rachel/Ivy drama for me. I suffered through about 12 hours of that until the story got interesting. And, I'm not seeing any real character growth so I'm taking an extended, maybe permanent break. It was tiresome seeing Rachel make the same dumb mistakes over and over again through five books. <br/><br/>On a brighter note, the narration is excellent. </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" B002RI9IZG" href="/book/show/23311477-for-a-few-demons-more">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">urban fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=tear-jerkers">tear-jerkers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22313662-lazaros?shelf=witches">witches</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1177586205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12136148320362797701"><i>
  <blockquote>“There were no more choices, no more options, no more clever ways out of a tough situation. And the rush, I realized in a brutal wash of despair, is a false god I’ve chased my entire life. One that cost me everything in the blind search for sensation. My entire existence amounted to nothing.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>I have no idea how I found the courage to read this book until it's very end. This one was full of suspense and a constant stress and a feeling that someone wouldn't come out of this alive, and for once,</span>
  <span id="freeText12136148320362797701" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“There were no more choices, no more options, no more clever ways out of a tough situation. And the rush, I realized in a brutal wash of despair, is a false god I’ve chased my entire life. One that cost me everything in the blind search for sensation. My entire existence amounted to nothing.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I have no idea how I found the courage to read this book until it's very end. This one was full of suspense and a constant stress and a feeling that someone wouldn't come out of this alive, and for once, I was right.. Someone did not get out alive.. <br /><br />Of course, I have to praise other elements in this novel as well, like the fact that by each book of this series I read I'm struck by how much character development there is. In a way, I'm reminded of those children books I've read where we grow up along with the characters. This series is like that, only it's not for kids, it's for grown-ups and it's targetting a more mature audience. I love how intertwined this is with real life elements but at the same time it's kept grounded to the paranormal. <br /><br />Rachel has grown so much on me since the first book. She's a great character and she's so caring. There's no boundaries where her friends' lives are concerned. No lengths she wouldn't go to for them in order to keep them alive and breathing. <br /><br />Ivy is one of the most powerful vampires, she's still a person though and she has feelings and she hurts and I'm sure by now that she is the most sensitive of our characters and I feel for her on so many levels. She is my favorite and I don't even have to justify myself.<br /><br />This book is the most personal one yet. I mean that it's just that our characters are a family now. It's like this tight family that deals with its problems as a team. Did they have to get separated? Yes. Did they have to work alone and make decisions alone? Yes. But ultimately they'd all be affected the same if one of them died.<br /><br />Should I go back to the death comment? No, I don't want to spoil you.. But the death shattered me.. I had grown to love this character. <br /><br />I hope the next book is more fun and less heartbreak even though I'm sure that whichever it is, I'm going to love it just the same.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12136148320362797701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6857324-lauren-stoolfire?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2540286768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12530390276764485906"><i>For A Few Demons More</i> (<i>The Hollows</i> #5) by Kim Harrison is the best book in the series so far. I've said it before and I'll say it again: Jenks is the real MVP. It's so cool to see Harrison's alternate Cincinnati. By the way, the short story included at the end of the novel called "The Bridges of Eden Park" was particularly brutal to read because of how the novel ended. How could Kim Harrison do that to us? I can't wait to continue this series. <i>The Outlaw Demon Wails</i>, here I come!</span>

<div id="review_1578797485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1578797485" />
    <a title="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer"><img alt="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375481031p2/3829694.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1578797485?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)" href="/user/show/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer">Mlpmom (Book Reviewer)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1578797485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5823276935110376727">It was so darn good to get back into this world. Even though I knew I loved this series, it was a huge reminder just why I love it.<br/><br/>Once again Rachel has gotten herself into a sticky situation. One full of danger, lies, and oh yeah, demons. The stakes are getting higher and not everyone is going to come out of this one alive. <br/><br/>There were so many feels with this, I don't even know where to begin. So much was revealed and said, and done. <br/><br/>I can't even begin to express how much I love this series. It </span>
  <span id="freeText5823276935110376727" style="display:none">It was so darn good to get back into this world. Even though I knew I loved this series, it was a huge reminder just why I love it.<br /><br />Once again Rachel has gotten herself into a sticky situation. One full of danger, lies, and oh yeah, demons. The stakes are getting higher and not everyone is going to come out of this one alive. <br /><br />There were so many feels with this, I don't even know where to begin. So much was revealed and said, and done. <br /><br />I can't even begin to express how much I love this series. It took me awhile to get into it, in fact three whole books before I completely felt the love but once that love blossomed, it really bloomed. <br /><br />I've seen others say this book was a turning point to the series and I absolutely agree. With all the things that happened it was impossible for anyone to come out of it the same. To be unchanged in some way or another. <br /><br />I don't want to spoil anything but I will say this, these friends, their bond and love for one another, is what makes this series so fantastic. I've always said that sometimes the best family are those we pick to be a part of instead of those we are sometimes born into and that is the case with Ivy, Jenks,and Rachel. There are so many good characters in this, great characters and of course even and some it's impossible not to hate with a fiery passion and I couldn't help but love Harrison for her ability to do that. <br /><br />If you are hesitating to try this series, don't. It's fantastic and even though like me, it might take you a bit to warm up to it, take that chance anyways, I don't think you'll regret it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5823276935110376727" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12894043?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/180427-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780061149818" href="/book/show/489454.For_a_Few_Demons_More">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12894043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13518098117646853426">Currently working my way through the requisite hundred or so pages of relationship angsting that has to happen before the plot starts. That may sound tedious, and frankly it is. But it's Harrison's pattern, and once the plot kicks into gear it's a fantastic ride. You just have to slog through that introductory angst first.<br/><br/>***<br/><br/>And now that I'm finished, I'm not sure what I think. The story itself was pretty darned exciting, but I'm getting a little sick of Rachel, and most of the people around her</span>
  <span id="freeText13518098117646853426" style="display:none">Currently working my way through the requisite hundred or so pages of relationship angsting that has to happen before the plot starts. That may sound tedious, and frankly it is. But it's Harrison's pattern, and once the plot kicks into gear it's a fantastic ride. You just have to slog through that introductory angst first.<br /><br />***<br /><br />And now that I'm finished, I'm not sure what I think. The story itself was pretty darned exciting, but I'm getting a little sick of Rachel, and most of the people around her. Her friends don't really seem to be her friends, they seem to be Ivy's friends, for all they worry about Ivy and how Ivy's going to react to this or that. I understand that Ivy's supposedly been through some crap in the past, but all her whining and moping, while everyone else tiptoes around her, has gotten really really old. I may be done with this series.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1976406453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1976406453" />
    <a title="Sara Kate" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21404261-sara-kate"><img alt="Sara Kate" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588645126p2/21404261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara Kate" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara Kate" href="/user/show/21404261-sara-kate">Sara Kate</a>

<div id="review_9414353" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9414353" />
    <a title="Joana Rodriguez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/634615-joana-rodriguez"><img alt="Joana Rodriguez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1195697348p2/634615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9414353?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joana Rodriguez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joana Rodriguez" href="/user/show/634615-joana-rodriguez">Joana Rodriguez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9414353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3278691876422106496">Wow. That was my final impression of the much anticipated fifth book in Kim Harrison’s Rachel Morgan series. Much like Harrison’s previous work, For a Few Demons More was a non-stop, action packed romp through an alternate version of Cincinnati. My only complaint was that the relationship of two of the main characters seems to have taken two steps back for the single step forward it gained. And of course the death of a beloved character never sits too well with anyone. But enough of the teasing.</span>
  <span id="freeText3278691876422106496" style="display:none">Wow. That was my final impression of the much anticipated fifth book in Kim Harrison’s Rachel Morgan series. Much like Harrison’s previous work, For a Few Demons More was a non-stop, action packed romp through an alternate version of Cincinnati. My only complaint was that the relationship of two of the main characters seems to have taken two steps back for the single step forward it gained. And of course the death of a beloved character never sits too well with anyone. But enough of the teasing.<br /><br />Poor Rachel, she’s a witch whose only desire was to become as good of a runner (a combination of investigator and bounty hunter) as her late father. But political machinations forced her to leave the I.S. and go it on her own. When she left she unknowingly took with her two new friends, Ivy Tamwood the last living Tamwood vampire and Jenks a temperamental pixie with a large family to care for. Throughout the series we’ve watched the friendship between this trio bloom as they overcame numerous obstacles set in their paths. Schemes were unraveled, trust betrayed and yet through it all they stuck it out and weathered the storm.<br /><br />Now in the fifth book the numerous conflicts that have been simmering beneath the surface all come to a boil. Newt, the powerful demon who strikes fear in the demon Al and the elf Ceri alike, and the same demon whose mark Rachel now carries as a price for being carried over the ley lines, comes after Rachel seeking something that she has and that Newt wants back. Problem is Newt can’t remember what it is she’s looking for. If a crazy demon isn’t scary enough add to that the fact that this demon can blasphemy the holy ground she walks on without a conscious effort. There is no safe hiding place from this demon. The trio suspect Newt wants the Focus, the werewolf artifact that Rachel got stuck with in the previous book, which means now they have to guard the artifact that could cause a war from the werewolves, the vampires, and a demon.<br /><br />At the same time the powerful and dangerous Trent Kalamack is getting married and wants Rachel to play bodyguard. After Newt’s visit she’s in dire need of money to fix the church and it’s really no surprise that she eventually caves and accepts Trent’s offer. We’ve seen that pattern before folks, her morals and ethics cause Rachel to tell Trent what he can do with his offers but in the end a combination of guilt over their father’s shared friendship, Trent’s father’s kindness, and sheer need usually force Rachel to give in. Maybe someday she’ll learn to save herself time and just accept the offer up front? After what happened in this book that’s not likely though.<br /><br />So Trent is getting married, Newt makes an appearance, and everyone is fighting for control of the focus, that alone is enough to make a good fifth installment. But Kim Harrison wouldn’t be the author she is today if she decided to do things half way. Every “villain” Rachel and company have had to contend with puts in an appearance. From a walking in the sun Al to a free and clear Piscary, they’re all back and there is a murder mystery to solve to boot. Just reading the book had my mind boggling at the stress and my nerves became frayed at the thought of dealing with everything Rachel had to contend with. Fans will be pleasantly surprised to see how Harrison wraps everything up, it’s not exactly what you would anticipate but it’s far from a let down. [...]<br /><br />- Yet again, my review is too long! You can <a href="http://review.nanashi-inc.net/?p=52" rel="nofollow noopener">read the full review here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3278691876422106496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_926471850" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926471850" />
    <a title="Kribu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5117138-kribu"><img alt="Kribu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307111631p2/5117138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/926471850?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kribu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kribu" href="/user/show/5117138-kribu">Kribu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5376553-for-a-few-demons-more">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=weres">weres</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5117138-kribu?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer926471850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10852107556274218679">It seems that <i>The Hollows</i> is a series that might just be a bit like crack: I don't find it that particularly awesome, and there's a lot about it that I don't in fact like, but overall, it's addictive and hard to stay away from - and dammit, I want more.<br/><br/>First, the bad: honestly? Pretty much the same things I've complained about in my reviews for the previous books. Epithets. Dear god, the epithets. There were long stretches where I either didn't notice them or an editor had got hold of some chunk</span>
  <span id="freeText10852107556274218679" style="display:none">It seems that <i>The Hollows</i> is a series that might just be a bit like crack: I don't find it that particularly awesome, and there's a lot about it that I don't in fact like, but overall, it's addictive and hard to stay away from - and dammit, I want more.<br /><br />First, the bad: honestly? Pretty much the same things I've complained about in my reviews for the previous books. Epithets. Dear god, the epithets. There were long stretches where I either didn't notice them or an editor had got hold of some chunks of the manuscript and removed them, but .. eurgh. Also, at least the UK edition seemed to have switched from Ceridwen to Cerdiwen consistently for Ceri's full name, and ... no. Just no.<br /><br />Various writing issues aside, I just... Rachel drives me up the wall. At least her characterisation has been consistent through the books, but dear god, how stupid can she be? This time we get her constant thoughts about her adrenaline-junky-ness and ... she still rushes to danger. All. The. Fucking. Time. ARGH. Add to that her questionable dress sense (shouldn't she by now have some inkling about what's appropriate for what occasion and what not??) and <i>her still bloody drooling after every single man/vampire/were/witch/demon she meets</i> (while having a steady boyfriend) and it's just. Argh. I <i>like</i> Rachel, in spite of everything, but god.<br /><br />Also, Ivy. This entire thing with Ivy. Thing is, I don't like Ivy. I've yet to find any reason whatsoever to like her, other than Rachel and Jenks and Kisten etc liking her. She's completely bland. Flat. No personality at all. I have no idea what she's about (other than really really really wanting to have sex with Rachel and drink her blood and what not). And frankly - while I appreciate having an urban fantasy series that has some diversity in the sexuality of the protagonists and has the protagonist consider that there might be some fluidity in her own sexuality - the entire Rachel/Ivy thing is just... not handled in a way that makes me like it, even the least bit. Blegh. On the plus side, at least Rachel is also aware of it possibly being just Ivy playing on the scar/vampire pheromones, but ... that is also really what bothers me. Ivy's basically drugging her every time she comes close and plays on the pheromones, and, eh.<br /><br />Also, Trent. I'm starting to get tired of how easily, all things considered, everyone - everyone who knows! - is brushing off his murderous tendencies. <br /><br />Good things: the plot, and Rachel's battling with the issues of demons, using demon curses, and the such. I like how she's starting to accept that things aren't always so black or white, and I'm curious to see where this is going.<br /><br />Also, Quen. And Minias! I loved Minias. I want more Minias. If the next books had nothing but Quen and Minias and Takata (I also want more Takata!), I'd be one happy camper. Sadly, I expect they won't, but hey, a girl can hope. And I was glad to see Glenn return, if in a smaller role! Actually, that is one thing I really appreciate about the series - minor/secondary characters from earlier books not just disappearing but remaining a part of the core cast's lives, returning or being mentioned now and again. Makes them feel like real people and not just props for the plot of a specific book.<br /><br />Will I be reading on? Absolutely. In spite of all my issues, I <i>am</i> enjoying the series. Just with a lot of headdesking involved.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10852107556274218679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I really don't know. How many people is she going to take down with her? While I did like reading to learn more about what is going on, I'm starting to really dislike this dumb bitch. <div id="review_311235120" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311235120" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311235120?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=magic-powers">magic-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=part-of-series">part-of-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311235120" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14985519153503160261">Book five is such an interesting blend. While it is one of the best in the series, likely the funniest, it is also the most tragic and depressing.<br/><br/>For the characters, a reader gets plenty of page time with their favorites. Al is around quite often but not in the typical fashion and for different reasons. There's the return of an older villain. Trent gets plenty of time on the page, as well, but this book soured my impressions of him. Even after reading all the books now up to book 12, I still fee</span>
  <span id="freeText14985519153503160261" style="display:none">Book five is such an interesting blend. While it is one of the best in the series, likely the funniest, it is also the most tragic and depressing.<br /><br />For the characters, a reader gets plenty of page time with their favorites. Al is around quite often but not in the typical fashion and for different reasons. There's the return of an older villain. Trent gets plenty of time on the page, as well, but this book soured my impressions of him. Even after reading all the books now up to book 12, I still feel soured. He turned me off for the first time with this book. <br /><br />Ivy is here but while I liked her before, her tragedy comes across as a bit irritating and overdone sometimes. She is certainly presented as fragile, but strong at the same time in other ways. Jenks is flying around and as impressive as always with his loyalty, humor, and genuine awesomeness. Kisten as the ultra boyfriend is here with a scene that was so hot to me the book almost started smoldering. <br /><br />The book excels with it's scenes. The wedding is seriously the funniest part of the series. It couldn't have been written better. I love re-reading it. The boat scene with Kisten was romantic and hot at the same time with a sweetness. Rachel is the ultimate badass - she's vulnerable and sensitive but does what she has to, even if her stomach is a jumble of nerves. She gets to shine here and finally accomplish something she's been itching for since the series started.<br /><br />For a few demons more digs deeper into the darker, gritty world of vampires. It's always been disturbing and twisted before, but now it's even worse. The true demented history is explored here for both Ivy and Kisten. Ugh. Even if there is much humor in this book, there is a darkness and seriousness to it that's unshakeable. <br /><br />The series takes a big turning point and things are never the same again. The ending of this book broke my heart. I was getting teary eyed a little the next day at work off and on, and that's nothing compared to actually reading sobering, surprising ending.<br /><br />I couldn't recommend the book higher if you're a series fan, but there's some emotional brutality waiting that angered me, depressed me, and turned the Hollows world upside down when I read it. With the book keeping its usual marriages of unusual plot arcs and this installment of the series holds consistent action. <br /><br />Exciting, fierce, inventive, hysterical, and then depressing as hell - For a Few Demons more is an excellent addition to the Hollows family.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14985519153503160261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_145888776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145888776" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145888776?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=hollows">hollows</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669344-jen-davis?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145888776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17663410406320859004">This book shredded me. I cried for the last 50 pages or so. And not just a silent tear or two, but out-loud crying... messy with used Kleenex all over the sofa. I will not spoil the why's of it, but I can't possibly talk about this book without acknowledging its enormous emotional impact. I don't know if I can ever forgive Kim Harrison.<br/><br/>With the ending weighing on me so heavily, it's hard to look back to the rest of the book. It starts out strong, addressing the repercussions of Rachel's interact</span>
  <span id="freeText17663410406320859004" style="display:none">This book shredded me. I cried for the last 50 pages or so. And not just a silent tear or two, but out-loud crying... messy with used Kleenex all over the sofa. I will not spoil the why's of it, but I can't possibly talk about this book without acknowledging its enormous emotional impact. I don't know if I can ever forgive Kim Harrison.<br /><br />With the ending weighing on me so heavily, it's hard to look back to the rest of the book. It starts out strong, addressing the repercussions of Rachel's interaction with the demon Newt. And as the story goes on, the focal point becomes a string of suspicious werewolf deaths. They turn out to be linked to the "focus," that statue Rachel got from Nick in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30260.A_Fistful_of_Charms__Rachel_Morgan_The_Hollows___4_" title="A Fistful of Charms (Rachel Morgan/The Hollows, #4) by Kim Harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">A Fistful of Charms</a>. It has the power to create new werewolves from humans --and now everyone wants it. And Rachel becomes everyone's target as they fight to get it. --I also have to mention... just when I though that maybe Trent wasn't a total slimeball, I've changed my mind again. He is.<br /><br />I always reread a series before a new installment comes out, but this is the book that made me dread re-reading the Hollows. Not because it's a bad book. On the contrary, it is incredibly powerful. I just remembered the ache it put in my chest the first time around --and even knowing what would happen, didn't ease the hurt the second time. If you're a fan of the series, you can't skip this one. Just have your Kleenex ready. 5 stars.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17663410406320859004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144606372" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144606372" />
    <a title="VampireNovelFan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4897902-vampirenovelfan"><img alt="VampireNovelFan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296445543p2/4897902.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=comedy">comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=elves">elves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4897902-vampirenovelfan?shelf=fae">fae</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144606372" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7483322698216396943">Not too far removed from Book 4, in For a Few Demons more we see that Rachel still has "the focus," a 5,000 year old demon-crafted werewolf artifact that was the focus of book 4. Considering its power, it's a hot commodity and everybody who is anybody wants to get their hands on it, from the evil Vampire Piscary to business tycoon and underground druglord, Trent Kalamack, to the Weres themselves. Rachel's got her hands full, and it doesn't help that her werewolf friend, David, is suspected of be</span>
  <span id="freeText7483322698216396943" style="display:none">Not too far removed from Book 4, in For a Few Demons more we see that Rachel still has "the focus," a 5,000 year old demon-crafted werewolf artifact that was the focus of book 4. Considering its power, it's a hot commodity and everybody who is anybody wants to get their hands on it, from the evil Vampire Piscary to business tycoon and underground druglord, Trent Kalamack, to the Weres themselves. Rachel's got her hands full, and it doesn't help that her werewolf friend, David, is suspected of being a serial by the FIB. How will Rachel get out of this one? Trent's long awaited wedding finally happens, but does it go down without a hitch?<br /><br />You'll have to read for yourself to find out. I know that a Fistful of Charms was a favorite for many, but as a self-professed fan of Kisten and Trent, this book was much more interesting for me since they get more focus. The previous book had one of the funniest moments ever in this series. Well, this book gives us another one. Let's just say that Rachel makes for a horrible bride's maid. That scene had me laughing out loud. <br /><br />I really like how this series has villains, but Harrison gives them qualities that keep them from being so one-dimensional. You want to get into their world and their perspective. And sometimes, Rachel's interactions with them can be either terrifying or downright hysterical, all in the course of one book. <br /><br />The scenes with Kisten were hott. I really like that this series adds a dash of romance, but it doesn't overtake the book. I've ran into a few favorites that start out being more about plot and then practically become erotica. <br /><br />A for how this book ends. I spoiled myself and opened up the last page, so I was prepared for the shock. If there's one thing you can say about Harrison; you gotta admit the woman's got balls!<br /><br />This is so far my favorite Urban Fantasy series so I highly recommend reading this book. Not every installment is as good as the the other, but this one is one of her best.<br /><br />*Review also posted to <a href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R25MI065LA6ERZ/ref=cm_cr_rdp_perm" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117980262" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117980262" />
    <a title="jD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2415283-jd"><img alt="jD" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1283353615p2/2415283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117980262?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jD" href="/user/show/2415283-jd">jD</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=magic_wizards-and-such">magic_wizards-and-such</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=magic_wide-range">magic_wide-range</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=series_paranormal">series_paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=fantasy_urban">fantasy_urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2415283-jd?shelf=2_kindle_own">2_kindle_own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117980262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9440908094229414010">I stopped about 100 pages into this one in Fall 2010 because I did not see enough character development. Had I continued to read it I don't think I would have come away with a different perspective because I wanted it too badly. I was reading it at the same time I was getting into Cat and Bones of Night Huntress so I wanted more of that. My opinion of what should happen overshadowed my ability to really enjoy what was. This time around, I was better prepared for the character short comings due t</span>
  <span id="freeText9440908094229414010" style="display:none">I stopped about 100 pages into this one in Fall 2010 because I did not see enough character development. Had I continued to read it I don't think I would have come away with a different perspective because I wanted it too badly. I was reading it at the same time I was getting into Cat and Bones of Night Huntress so I wanted more of that. My opinion of what should happen overshadowed my ability to really enjoy what was. This time around, I was better prepared for the character short comings due to spoilers. Yes, for some of us spoilers sell the book.<br /><br />I really enjoyed the early installments to the series which I read years ago. The Hollows was my first witch series and I loved many aspects of the writing and magic. I found Rachael interesting but I did not like Ivy from jump. The dysfunctional abusive relationship between these two got on my nerves. As for boyfriends, I felt Rachael was living below her potential with her broke lovers when she was broke herself. Nobody around her but Jenks, a pixie, had any maturity thus Rachael did not grow as a person. She went from one bad decision to the next. After three books I just didn't see change on the horizon but I was wrong.<br /><br />"For A Few Demons More" proved to me that Rachael's journey was not destined to be perpetual stupidity and self-destruction. There is plenty in this book but it served a higher purpose, Rachael moved forward, finally. There was plenty of the good stuff such as Rachael's quick wit and her compassion. She did some stupid stuff and some of the stupid decisions from earlier books came back to bite her in the ass. But by the conclusion, she realized her actions were wreckless and did some growing up. I even got a little more comfortable with Ivy although if Ms. Harrison kills her off, I'm good with that too. If Ivy and Rachael become lovers, I am done. Jenx is a treat, as always. Kristen is the same -- no money, no power, and not a drop of Alpha in him. Rachael loves him and he treats her good so I won't dwell on him. I am looking forward to reading more about Ceri the elf Rachael rescued from Never Never. Trent's hot and rich but Rachael hates him with a passion. I don't see that changing anytime soon based on this book. He is a bad guy but I wouldn't mind Rachael taking him out for a test drive. The consequences of dabbling with demons comes full circle. Rachael needed the hard knocks that came with the reality of how deep she had gotten with the demons. There is also something going on with that cat...I am sure of it. <br /><br />Best scene in the book was when Trent said to Rachael -- "You should have killed Piscary when you had the opportunity." Thank you Trent. I love you even if Rachael doesn't. <br /><br />All in all, I really liked this installment. Ms. Harrison is a talented Urban Fantasy writer who does not shy away from violence. Her magicical world is ripe with opportunity for what I expect to ba a long running series. I am looking forward to reading the next one.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9440908094229414010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10261134200745143036">I'm exasperated with myself for loving this series so much, but I do. And this book is where it really starts to take off. <br/><br/>Rachel is still infuriatingly idiotic, with horrible, horrible taste in fashion and even worse impulse control. She's not quite as naive as she was in the first couple books, but there are still moments when I feel like giving her a good Gibbs slap. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581273191ra/28935515.gif' width='480' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The first time I read this, it really hit me hard when <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[a bad, bad thing happens <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. This time, not </span>
  <span id="freeText10261134200745143036" style="display:none">I'm exasperated with myself for loving this series so much, but I do. And this book is where it really starts to take off. <br><br>Rachel is still infuriatingly idiotic, with horrible, horrible taste in fashion and even worse impulse control. She's not quite as naive as she was in the first couple books, but there are still moments when I feel like giving her a good Gibbs slap. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1581273191ra/28935515.gif" width="480" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first time I read this, it really hit me hard when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a bad, bad thing happens <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. This time, not so much. I'm having a difficult time getting behind any of Rachel's relationships, the one with Kiston included. She <i>says</i> she loves him, but I'm just not buying it. I feel absolutely nothing for these two. Maybe it's because Rachel throws her so-called love around like she's tossing candy out in a parade--Nick, Ivy, and now Kiston--but it could also be because he has all of two scenes in the book (and barely any in previous books), and their interactions have very little depth. But it could also be because I've finished the series and know what happens next. And then next. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Can't wait. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Meanwhile we are still dealing with Ivy/Rachel angst, and I thought it was finally going to be resolved by this point? Sigh. The situation there is so totally contrived and with so much false-drama that I cringe while reading. I should have marked passages so that if I ever read this again I know exactly what to skip (note to self for future installments). <br><br>Stupid heroine and bad relationships aside, Harrison really knows how to entertain a girl. The book is action-packed and filled with so many funny moments and comments (mostly from Jenks) that I laugh out loud. I could listen to a thousand of his Tinkerbell jokes and never be bored.<br><br><i>"Good god the man is dumber than Tinks' dildo.</i><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587834743ra/29356733.gif" width="480" height="365" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Pretty sure Walt is turning in his grave.<br><br>The plots are well thought-out and I always love when Trent is involved...the man I love to hate should be featured in every single book. Ciri is the perfect badass, demon-trained, scary fairy princess and the scene where she shows her true colors and puts Trent in his place is perfect. Gotta love the elves. <br><br>Can't wait to read what happens next. And then next. Because Al is gonna be <i>pissed,</i> and that is always a good time!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1587834956ra/29356737.gif" width="480" height="480" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_188489618" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/188489618" />
    <a title="Tabitha " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5863594-tabitha"><img alt="Tabitha " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513129123p2/5863594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/188489618?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tabitha " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tabitha " href="/user/show/5863594-tabitha">Tabitha </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5376553-for-a-few-demons-more">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer188489618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17785397982567122087">This review is also featured on <a href='https://www.behindthepages.org/post/for-a-few-demons-more-by-kim-harrison' rel='nofollow noopener'>Behind the Pages: For A Few Demons More</a><br/><br/><b>It was as if a part of me had died, accepting that I couldn’t be who I wanted, so I had to work at making who I was, someone I could live with.</b><br/><br/>Rachel is going to have to accept demons are going to ruin her life. Every time she turns around, a demon seems to be crossing the lines to pester her. Of course, it doesn’t help that she’s learning how to spin curses from Ceri. But if a curse doesn’t hurt someone, it isn’t evil right?</span>
  <span id="freeText17785397982567122087" style="display:none">This review is also featured on <a href="https://www.behindthepages.org/post/for-a-few-demons-more-by-kim-harrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Behind the Pages: For A Few Demons More</a><br /><br /><b>It was as if a part of me had died, accepting that I couldn’t be who I wanted, so I had to work at making who I was, someone I could live with.</b><br /><br />Rachel is going to have to accept demons are going to ruin her life. Every time she turns around, a demon seems to be crossing the lines to pester her. Of course, it doesn’t help that she’s learning how to spin curses from Ceri. But if a curse doesn’t hurt someone, it isn’t evil right? As Rachel tries to help the FIB solve a case of suicidal weres, she’ll have to fend off the demons that come knocking. She’ll also have to live through Trent Kalamack’s wedding, and true to Rachel’s style she’ll cause quite the commotion.<br /><br />If you’ve been following along with my reread of The Hollows, then you know how much I love the series. So why did I take away a star? I will fully admit it’s because this book was slower than the previous novels and felt a bit disjointed. There’s a lot less action and a lot more drama.<br /><br />Kim will go into detail on the differences between ley line magic and demon curses. You’ll also learn more about the demons to set the foundation for future novels. There’s not going to be a lot of action as far as runs go. There are quite a few subplots in the story, and I don’t think there was space left over for a run.<br /><br />There’s a lot of moving from place to place. Rachel has a lot on her plate this time, and I just didn’t feel the adrenaline filled character I’d come to know. The FIB calling her in to help investigate was a break from the norm. Even Rachel says she isn’t an investigator. She’s more of a tag them and bag them person.<br /><br />But, this is an important book in the series, so make sure you stick with it. Rachel is slowly becoming a person who is sure of themselves and realizes the world can't be painted in black and white.<br /><br />That being said, this was one of the first books to make me bawl my eyes out. I even wrote to Kim years ago telling her she wrote it beautifully, and she broke my heart in the process. She sent me a memorandum of who we'd lost as a fan base, and to this day I treasure it.<br /><br />Buckle up and give it a try. I feel like every series has at least one book that doesn’t quite sit well, but that doesn’t mean the journey isn’t worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17785397982567122087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_73808708" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/73808708" />
    <a title="valee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2320890-valee"><img alt="valee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443365004p2/2320890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73808708?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="valee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="valee" href="/user/show/2320890-valee">valee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007247790" href="/book/show/610835.For_a_Few_Demons_More">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2320890-valee?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73808708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6602783122612901250">For me this installment in the series wasn't as good as the last 2 books, which were a 5 stars-rating and favs. I would give this book 3.5 stars if possible.<br/><br/>The beginning was good. All the drama with Al was a great way to begin the book. I like him a lot. He's not one of my fav characters but a really good one; you just know that if he's in the picture thing will get juicy. <br/><br/>My problem was that then things got slower and slower. It took me forever to finish it. I got bored more than once and had </span>
  <span id="freeText6602783122612901250" style="display:none">For me this installment in the series wasn't as good as the last 2 books, which were a 5 stars-rating and favs. I would give this book 3.5 stars if possible.<br /><br />The beginning was good. All the drama with Al was a great way to begin the book. I like him a lot. He's not one of my fav characters but a really good one; you just know that if he's in the picture thing will get juicy. <br /><br />My problem was that then things got slower and slower. It took me forever to finish it. I got bored more than once and had to stop reading it. I never felt like I couldn't stop reading the book, only at the last 40 pages. And 40 pages in almost 500 isn't much. I didn't like also some other things that happened in this book. The way things changed between Rache and Ivy wasn't how I pictured it. I mean make up your minds, or you get together or you don't, but a whole book doubting it was damn boring. I just wanted things to go back the way they used to be. I didn't care much for the general plot as well. The thing with the wolves focus was boring as hell. And Trent passed from being my fav character to the biggest jackass on Earth.<br /><br />I would have given 4 stars to this one because the ending was really good, as always, and everything that happened to Kist really got to me. I also think that Harrison was able to fix everything that was annoying me at the end, so I may be enjoying more the next book. But with all the things I mentioned for why I didn't enjoy this book as much as the other I just can't give 4 stars to it.<br /><br />I still love this series and totally recommend it. Jenks, Ivy and Rachel are amazing characters. I think this series is the only one I have read without any romance in it and enjoyed. I usually don't like series with no romance, but this one has things that compensate it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6602783122612901250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10759416542677537379" style="display:none">June 28, 2020: Knowing what will happen makes this book so much more difficult to listen to. 😢. Trent is a real a— in this one. <br /><br />July 7, 2019: This is one of my least favorite books in the series because, Kisten. 😥<br /><br />Rachel Morgan is a kick ass witch who is always getting herself into trouble. With the help of her friends, she must always create interesting solutions to get herself out of the messes she creates for herself. She has a difficult time trusting people and men in particular. Throughout the series, she learns to love and trust. If Rachel sounds like you or any other woman you know, these books are fun to read. Harrison creates an intriguing background by using the division of Cincinnati over Ohio and Kentucky. I read the entire series in less than a week because I could not put the books down.</span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rPOj6ccYBlWaHVDgFyZLjbyJH61NkRFd1UtwKdYL2yKKT+aw9EyyHj3cPqFML+8w/JybJNGmdyIsbTMtwv6RMg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vPmL684lhHJ5MYAOvdZ9Jdw+P/fsekIzdU16w85Pp+WaRc6y/XEwOd7w7k/m39mYnCu7fnBNJEyMaznH2rrt9Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

  <span id="freeText12806560265634245021" style="display:none">Kim Harrison is best known as the author of the New York Times #1 best selling Hollows series, but she has written more than urban fantasy and has published over two-dozen books spanning the gamut from young adult, thriller, several anthologies, and has scripted two original graphic novels. She has also published traditional fantasy under the name Dawn Cook. Kim is currently working on a new Hollows book between other, non related, urban fantasy projects.<br />Kim reaches out to her audience at Facebook <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/KimHarrisonsHollows?ref=ts">https://www.facebook.com/KimHarrisons...</a> <br />Instagram<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://instagram.com/kim_harrison_author/">https://instagram.com/kim_harrison_au...</a><br />and her blog <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://kimharrison.wordpress.com/">http://kimharrison.wordpress.com/</a><br /><br /><b>other pseudonyms:</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/64216.Dawn_Cook" rel="nofollow noopener">Dawn Cook</a></span>

And no one else."<br />"Ow!" I exclaimed, trying to yank my fingers from Trent but finding them caught. Then I colored, realizing what I'd said. "Oh… sorry," I stammered, meaning it. "That was insensitive."<br />Trent's frown turned into a sly smirk. "Bump uglies?" he said, eyes on the table behind me. "You are a font of gutter slang, Rachel. We must do this again.&rdquo;</span>
